## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or coupling terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) + c2 * v (time-modulated stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (coupled nonlinear terms)
- Helmholtz-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic restoring)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * v (multiplicative coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells; even powers (x²) → asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/driving)
- Terms like (1 - c*x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators (Van der Pol type)
- Explicit time dependence via sin/cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Products x*v suggest velocity-dependent restoring forces or position-dependent damping
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same sign as linear term x → hardening spring; opposite sign → softening spring
- Absence of explicit time dependence t suggests an autonomous system where energy considerations constrain the form
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative with a potential energy function V(x)

These are different when v < 0: v³ is negative, v*|v| is also negative (since |v| > 0, sign follows v). Actually v*|v| = sign(v)*v² and v³ = v*v², so v*|v| = v³/|v|*|v| ... Let me think again.

v³: if v > 0, v³ = v³. If v < 0, v³ < 0. So v³ ≠ v*|v| in general.

Wait - let me reconsider v³ vs v*|v|. v*|v| when v > 0 gives v², when v < 0 gives -v². Meanwhile v³ when v > 0 gives v³, when v < 0 gives -|v|³. These are fundamentally different functions.
